In the first column are 73 patients who were classed as shown in last year's report and have not attended this year. It will be seen that 469 of the 726 cases are under treatment, while in 1913 there were 270, so that there is an increase of 199. 300 were under treatment at one of the dispensaries, compared with 203 last year, and 169 under treatment elsewhere, compared with 67 last year. It is gratifying that the number under treatment elsewhere has increased much more than the number under dispensary treatment, as it shows that treatment in institutions and by the patients own medical practitioners have been employed to a greater extent, and there are many cases which from the first require these forms of treatment more than dispensary treatment. In estimating the permanent effect of treatment in a disease of so long a duration as Tuberculosis, it is necessary to keep patients under observation for a year or two after apparent cure or improvement in symptoms. At present the dispensaries have not been open sufficiently long for an accurate estimate. I have, however, made an attempt to summarise the results to date in some of the cases, and for this purpose have chosen the 300 cases who were under treatment at the dispensaries at the end of 1914. The duration of treatment varies from 21 months to a few weeks, according to the date of the first attendance of the patient. Of the 300 cases, 127 have shown definite signs of improvement, 127 have remained in a stationary condition, and in 46 the disease has advanced. 148 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Tuberculin Treatment. Tuberculin and Spengler's immune substances, I.K., have been used in some of the cases. As regards the former, opportunity for its use is limited by the fact that a large number of the most suitable cases, the early ones, take advantage of the Sanatorium treatment now available. Nor does one feel justified in advising otherwise, as change of air, rest and good food, are in many cases invaluable. Were the residence in Sanatoria of longer duration, it is felt that the results would be more lasting. Tuberculin has been used in some pulmonary cases and in some of tuberculous infection of glands with good results. Of the above-mentioned 300 cases, 24 received treatment with Tuberculin, 14 improving, eight remaining stationary, and two advancing under the treatment. In some of the more advanced cases Spengler's I.K. has been used with benefit and in some febrile cases in children it has been found to effect a reduction in temperature with benefit to the general health. The cases treated by this method are usually more advanced than those treated with tuberculin, so that one does not expect the results to be as good. 33 of the 300 cases were so treated, 12 improving, seven remaining stationary and 14 advancing under the treatment. I.K. is devoid of certain disadvantages attending the use of tuberculin in dispensary practice and it is hoped that when the cases treated with it have been under observation for a longer period, it will be possible to record more good results. 149 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Bacteriological Examination of Sputum. 384 examinations of sputum were made at the Lister Institute : 46 from Clapham, 26 from Putney, 123 from Streatham, 55 from Tooting, and 134 from Wandsworth. In 98 of the cases it was reported that the bacillus had been found, and in 286 that it was absent. Other Infective Diseases 33 deaths were caused by other Infective diseases, four in Clapham, 14 in Streatham, six in Tooting, and nine in Wandsworth. 11 of these were under one year, one from one and under two years, one from five and under 15 years, 13 from 25 and under 45 years, five from 45 and under 65 years, and two over 65 years. Of these 19 were stated to have been due to Syphilis, nine to Septicaemia, two to Tetanus, one to English Cholera, one to Dysentry, and one to Cerebro-spinal Meningitis. With regard to the number of deaths from Syphilis, 12 were Congenital Syphilis, and seven were of adults from Cerebral Syphilis. 10 deaths were caused by Syphilis in 1913, and 17 in 1912. The number of deaths from this disease, however, give little information as to the general prevalence of venereal diseases among the community, as it is more than probable that a considerable number of the deaths of infants from Congenital Debility and Marasmus is due to this cause. It is now, however, generally recognised that what are entitled the para-syphilitic diseases as General Paralysis of the Insane and Locomotor Ataxy are later manifestations of Syphilis, and if the number of deaths from these is taken as a criterion a more reliable estimate may be arrived at. 151 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. In 1914, the number of deaths from General Paralysis was 27, and from Locomotor Ataxy 10, a total of 37, 29 of males and eight of females. In 1913 the number of deaths from General Paralysis was 31, and from Locomotor Ataxy 10, a total of 41, 23 of males and eight of females. Ophthalmia Neonatorum. 51 cases were notified, of which nine were in Clapham, four in Putney, 21 in Streatham, five in Tooting and 12 in Wandsworth. 48 of the cases were visited, in one case no inquiries were made, 21 were attended at birth by midwives, nine were treated at hospital as out-patients, one as an in-patient, and four were removed to the Union Infirmary, the 24 remaining being treated at home. One case is still under treatment. Two cases removed and could not be traced, and four died of Convulsions, Heart disease, congenital debility and specific disease, respectively. The 41 remaining cases have recovered. One child, aged nine weeks, came from Liverpool on September 1st and was removed to the Infirmary on September 3rd., the case being notified from there. It was still an in-patient at the end of year. Of the two cases under treatment at the end of 1913, one infant has lost the sight of one eye, but the other eye is clear, and the other child has recovered. The Public Health (Ophthalmia Neonatorium) Regulations, 1914, came into force on the 1st April, by which midwives in addition to Medical Practitioners were required to notify cases occurring during their attendance on the mother and child. Violence. 113 deaths, 77 of males and 36 of females, occurred from Violence, compared with 115 in 1913, 116 in 1912, and 120 in 1911. 86 of the deaths were due to Accidental, and 22 to Suicidal causes. Five deaths were caused by other forms of Violence, one being a child belonging to Clapham who was killed during the bombardment of Scarborough, and the other four were of soldiers who died in England from wounds received in action. 16 of the deaths belonged to Clapham, 16 to Putney, 43 to Streatham, 15 to Tooting, and 23 to Wandsworth. During the year 47 notices with respect to 42 premises were received from the Water Board stating that the supply had been withdrawn. Eight of the premises were in Clapham, 12 in Putney, 11 in Streatham, three in Tooting, and eight in Wandsworth. The supply was withdrawn for non-payment of rates from 17 premises, from 13 premises in consequence of defects, and in 12 the premises were empty. Compared with 1913, there has been a decrease of 18 in the number of notices received, and of 31 in the number of premises affected. Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 169 Mortuaries. The Mortuaries in Clapham, Streatham, Tooting and Wandsworth have been visited several times during the year, and I am able to report that the By-laws and Regulations have been carried out in a satisfactory manner. With reference to the Wandsworth Mortuary the Public Health Committee have on several occasions had the question of providing a new Mortuary for Wandsworth before them, and plans have been prepared and laid before the Committee, but owing to the war the matter has been postponed. The Mortuary at Tooting has been closed, but a temporary one has been provided pending the erection of a new one in Wandsworth. in Clapham, 29 bodies were removed to the Mortuary, compared with 40 in 1913; in Streatham 46, compared with 51; and in Wandsworth 115, of which 57 were from Wandsworth, 32 from Putney, seven from Streatham and 19 from Tooting, compared with 114 in 1913—a total of 190 compared with 205 in 1913. No infectious cases were admitted to any of the Mortuaries during the year. GENERAL SANITARY WORK IN 1914. The following list shows the special inspections made by me during the year:— (i)—Special inspection was made of the land at the rear of Ravensbury Road in the Borough of Wimbledon on account of complaints as to damp conditions arising from the flooding of the land for use as a Skating pond. I inspected the land with the Medical Officer of Health for Wimbledon, but could find no nuisance to any premises in this Borough arising from the 170 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. flooding. The boundary ditch was also inspected and steps were taken to have this cleaned out so as to remove any serious obstruction to the flow of water in the ditch. The land has now been raised about six feet and consequently no further flooding can be carried out. The ditch has been inspected on several occasions since and no nuisance found. (2)—Special inspections were also made of certain houses and localities on account of flooding after the severe storm of June 14th. The streets chiefly affected were, in Putney—Campion Street and Upper Richmond Road; in Streatham—Besley Street, Broadway, Christchurch Road, Hambro Road, High Road, Hopton Road, Killieser Avenue, Mitcham Lane, Wellfield Road, Calbourne Road, Fernlea Road, Gosberton Road, Mayford Road, Ravenslea Road, Rossiter Road, Rowfant Road, Selkirk Road, and Tantallon Road; in Tooting—Defoe Road, Furzedown Market, Marlborough House and Mitcham Road; and in Wandsworth—Bellew Terrace, Earlsfield Road, Garratt Lane, Headworth Road, Lydden Grove, Maskell Road, Portinscale Road, Rusholme Road and Summerstown. Steps were taken at once to remedy the damp conditions and the officials of the Council both from this Department and the Surveyors assisted the owners and occupiers of the houses in every possible way. Many basements were cleansed and disinfected by the Council's staff, and in about 14 days all the cases had been satisfactorily dealt with. There was no consequent illness in any of these houses as far as could be ascertained. (3)—As in previous years, special inspections were made of several localities in consequence of complaints of smells from road gullies and sewer ventilators. The number of complaints was greater than in the previous year ; this having been due to the fact that the climatic conditions were more favourable. in all, 138 complaints were received, compared with 90 in 1913: three from Clapham North, three from Clapham Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 171 South, 11 from Putney, 34 from Streatham, 13 from Balham, 20 from Tooting, 22 from Southfield, nine from Fairfield, and 23 from Springfield Wards. All these complaints were forwarded to the Borough Engineer, who reported that in 112 cases the sewers were flushed and disinfected, in 17 the manholes were temporarily sealed, in seven ventilating columns were erected, while in two cases broken manhole plates were repaired. (4)—Special inspections were also made by myself and the Deputy Medical Officer of Health of many premises, chiefly on account of nuisances and damp conditions reported to the Sanitary inspectors and also to ascertain if any of these premises could be reported to the Council under the Housing, Town Planning, etc., Act, and also the by-laws as to Underground Rooms, made under the above Act. (5)—Special inspection was made of the Osiers, Point Pleasant, Wandsworth, owing to the outbreak of Swine fever and the necessary slaughtering of swine at the piggeries. All the work carried ont, both as regards slaughtering, cleansing and disinfection was satisfactory. including the house-to-house inspections and inspections for certificates under the Revenue Act, but excluding the routine inspection of bakehouses, slaughter-houses, cowsheds, and offensive trade premises, 380 inspections were made of premises, chiefly previous to the service of statutory notices. My attendance at the Police Court was necessary on four occasions during the year. Revenue Act. During the year 10 certificates were granted under the above Act, one deferred, and three refused. The certificates granted referred to 47 houses or 95 tenements, that deferred to eight houses or 16 tenements, and those refused to 38 houses or 76 tenements. 172 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Mousing. Town Planning, etc., Act, 1909. All the house-to-house inspections during the year have again been carried out under and for the purposes of Section 17 of this Act, and the results of these inspections have been recorded on the cards, particulars of which were given in the Report for 1910. it has not been found necessary to take any action under this Act, as it has been found, after careful consideration and personal inspection, that the nuisances detected could all be dealt with under the Public Health (London) Act, 1891. The tables of house-to-house inspections show, as in former years, the name of the street, the number of houses inspected, the number of houses in which defects were found, and the number of families living in one, two, three, and four rooms and upwards. The defects found are given in the Table of Sanitary Operations, as also the number of intimation and statutory notices served and complied with. Underground Rooms. Several inspections were made of property to ascertain if any additional underground rooms existed, but no cases were this year discovered in which there was illegal occupation of such rooms. All the houses erected for occupation by the working classes during the past 15 years have no basements, and consequently the number of underground rooms in this Borough is very small. Sanitary Operations. Tables LXXXIX., XC., and XCI., show the number and nature of the inspections made during the year by the Male and Female inspectors respectively. These Tables show in more detail the varied character of the work carried out by the inspectors. Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 173 The number of complaints received and attended to was 2,548, compared with 2,394 in 1913. 2,528 in 1912, and 2,076 in 1911. There was an increase in Clapham North and South, Streatham, Southfield, and Fairfield Wards, and a decrease in Putney, Balham, Tooting, and Springfield Wards, compared with the previous year. Three of these complaints were made to the London County Council, and these were at once attended to. The number of houses and premises inspected was 40,004, an increase of 1,201 compared with 1913, and of 3,668 compared with 1912. There was an increase in the number of houses and premises inspected in Clapham North and South, Putney, Balham, Tooting, Southfield, Fairfield, and Springfield Wards, and a decrease in Streatham Ward. The total number of house-to-house inspections made was 2,396, compared with 2,739 in 1913, 2,674 in 1912, and 2,486 in 1911. There has been an increase in the number of these inspections in Clapham North, Streatham, and Balham Wards, and a decrease in Clapham South, Putney, Tooting, Southfield, Fairfield, and Springfield Wards, compared with 1913. The number of these inspections has diminished owing to the changes in the inspectorial staff on account of the war, and the necessary inspections in some of the sub-districts of premises occupied by the military. 174 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. The total number of intimation notices served was 5,897, compared with 6,305 in 1913, 6,620 in 1912, and 6,278 in 1911, and of statutory notices 406, compared with 540, 707, and 957. The greatest number of intimation notices was served in Streatham, Balham and Springfield Wards, and the smallest number in Southfield and Putney Wards. The greatest number of statutory notices was served in Balham and Springfield Wards and the smallest number in Putney and Tooting Wards. Only 32 of the statutory notices, six in Clapham, two in Putney, 18 in Streatham, and six in Wandsworth, served in 1914, were not complied with at the close of the year. 29 of these notices were complied with in the beginning of the current year, with regard to one the premises are unoccupied, while in one the work is in hand, and in one a closing order has been obtained. The number of statutory notices served include By-law notices, 131 of which were served in respect of the following contraventions of the By-laws :—Yard paving 23, repairs to water closets 13, repairs to flushing apparatus of water closets 20, cleansing of water closets one, covers to cisterns six, cleansing cisterns eight, cleansing house and other contraventions of the By-laws as to houses let in lodgings 53, absence of cover to manure receptacle three, and failing to deposit manure in a proper receptacle four. The number of cases of overcrowding dealt with during the year was 81, compared with 75 in 1913, 76 in 1912, and 91 in 1911. 11 of these were in Clapham, two in Putney, 19 in Streatham, six in Tooting, and 43 in Wandsworth. The cases of overcrowding in Clapham were in Rashleigh Street, Crichton Street, Nursery Street, Nelson's Row, Upper Orchard Street, Park Crescent, Carfax Square and Clapham Park Road ; in Putney in Floss Street ; in Streatham, in Nimrod Road, Fallsbrook Road, Roupell Buildings, Greyhound Square, Mill Lane, Zennor Road, Larch Road, Fernlea Road, Balham New Road, Hazelhurst Road and Hereward Road ; in Tooting, in Khartoum Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 189 Road, Rookstone Road, Himley Road and Gilbey Road ; in Wandsworth, in Penwith Road, Brandlehow Road, Pier Terrace, Guelph Street, Jew's Row, Twilley Street, Bridgefield Grove, Ballantine Street, Malva Road, York Road, Garratt Lane, Vermont Street, Ferrier Street, Baylin Road, Aslett Street, Bendon Valley, Beechcroft Road, Dunt's Hill Road, Thornsett Road, Maskell Road, Atheldene Road, and Cubitts Cottages. Most of these were cases of domestic overcrowding and were remedied without difficulty by re-arrangement of the sleeping accommodation, while in several cases lodgers had been taken in by the tenants and these removed. 1,860 ashpits were provided or repaired, compared with 1,052 in 1913, 717 in 1912, and 831 in 1911. 289 complaints with reference to the non-removal of house refuse (45 from Clapham, 47 from Putney, 95 from Streatham, nine from Tooting, and 93 from Wandsworth), were received during the year. These complaints were, as in previous years, attended to by the Dusting Inspectors. 869 yards in connection with dwelling-houses, and 116 in connection with stables, were paved, drained, or cleansed, compared with 959 and 65 in 1913. 4,896 rooms and 911 staircases and passages were cleansed or repaired, compared with 5,388 rooms and 1,207 staircases and passages in 1913. The greatest number of rooms cleansed was in the Balham Ward, where 1,123 were done, and in Fairfield Ward, where 667 were done, and the smallest number in Southfield and Putney where the numbers were 255 and 271 respectively. 1,025 drains were cleansed or repaired, and 98 rain-water pipes disconnected from the drains. 101 notices of reconstruction of drains were sent to the Borough Engineer from this Department : 24 in Clapham, compared with 21 in 1913 ; four in Putney, compared with five ; 41 in Streatham, compared with 53 ; nine in Tooting, compared with 10 ; and 23 in Wandsworth, compared with 56. 190 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. The total number of houses where the drains were reconstructed during the year was 192 : 54 in Clapham, 10 in Putney, 76 in Streatham, 12 in Tooting, and 40 in Wandsworth. During the year 3,539 drains of houses were tested by the Sanitary Inspectors, 884 in Clapham, 266 in Putney, 1,182 in Streatham, 199 in Tooting, and 1,008 in Wandsworth, and 473 or 13.3 per cent. were found to be defective. Of the 473 found defective, 44 or five per cent. were in Clapham, 36 or 13.5 per cent. in Putney, 208 or 17.6 per cent. in Streatham, 81 or 40.7 per cent. in Tooting, and 104 or 10.3 per cent. in Wandsworth. 329 accumulations of manure were removed after service of notice, compared with 289 in 1913 : 40 in Clapham, 50 in Putney, 86 in Streatham, 67 in Tooting, and 86 in Wandsworth. There has been an increase in the number of cases dealt with in Putney, Streatham, Tooting, and Wandsworth, and a decrease in Clapham and Streatham. Three notices were served for the periodical removal of manure every 48 hours, compared with 15 in 1913, eight in 1912, and 12 in 1911. The number of water closets cleansed and repaired was 1,511, compared with 1,764 in 1913. The greatest number of these were in Balham and Springfield Wards, and the smallest in Putney and Southfield Wards. 412 drinking water cisterns were cleansed, covered or repaired: 100 in Clapham, 17 in Putney, 138 in Streatham, 42 in Tooting, and 115 in Wandsworth, compared with 527 in 1913. 105 premises were inspected and notices served where animals were kept in such a manner as to be a nuisance. Four of these were in Clapham, four in Putney, 28 in Streatham, 12 in Tooting, and 57 in Wandsworth. This nuisance was most common in Fairfield and Springfield Wards, and the animals kept were chiefly ducks and hens, Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 191 79 smoke nuisances were reported during the year : five in Clapham, four in Putney, six in Streatham, one in Tooting, and 63 in Wandsworth. In all 331 observations for black smoke were made by the Inspectors, 79 nuisances were reported and 49 notices served. Four complaints of black smoke were received from the Public Control Department of the London County Council with regard to four premises, and three complaints from the Coal Smoke Abatement Society with regard to four premises. These complaints were all at once attended to and the premises kept under observation. 143 soil pipes were repaired, 27 in Clapham, eight in Putney, 70 in Streatham, 23 in Tooting, and 15 in Wandsworth, compared with 119 in 1913, 159 in 1912, and 194 in 1911. 725 leaky roofs and gutters were repaired, compared with 746 in 1913, 870 in 1912, and 869 in 1911. 22 unwholesome or dilapidated houses were cleansed and repaired, six in Putney, two in Streatham, and 14 in Wandsworth compared with 23 in 1913, 60 in 1912, and 30 in 1911. A large amount of work has again been carried out to abate nuisances arising from damp conditions. In all, 606 premises have been dealt with, 74 in Clapham, 22 in Putney, 286 in Streatham, 65 in Tooting, and 159 in Wandsworth ; and in 199 of these, 24 in Clapham, six in Putney, 68 in Streatham, 11 in Tooting, and 90 in Wandsworth, damp courses have been inserted. The number of unclassified nuisances was 849, 285 in Clapham, 56 in Putney, 247 in Streatham, 59 in Tooting, and 202 in Wandsworth, compared with 947 in 1913, 929 in 1912, and 765 in 1911, 192 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Disinfection. The total number of rooms disinfected after the occurrence of cases of infectious disease was 4,030 (604 in Clapham, 456 in Putney, 1,160 in Streatham, 441 in Tooting, and 1,269 in Wandsworth), compared with 4,404 in 1913, 3,787 in 1912, and 4,419 in 1911. 2,268 lots of bedding were stoved at the Disinfecting Station, compared with 1,801 in 1913, 1,744 in 1912, and 1,603 in 1911. The 2,268 lots of bedding included the following :—1,379 beds, 1,429 bolsters, 3,196 pillows, 1,586 mattresses, 393 palliasses, 2,706 sheets, 1,883 quilts, 543 cushions, 8,198 articles of clothing, 4,103 blankets, 123 carpets, and 3,272 extra articles, a total of 28,809 articles, compared with 23,101 in 1913, 21,401 in 1912, and 21,613 in 1911. 372 premises were disinfected after Measles and 399 after Pulmonary Tuberculosis, compared with 1,454 and 420 in 1913. 34 beds, 22 bolsters, 59 pillows, 71 mattresses, 50 palliasses, 17 sheets, four quilts, 32 cushions, 216 articles of clothing, 14 blankets, 10 carpets, and 122 extra articles, were removed and destroyed by request of the owners during the year. Disinfection was also carried out by the Sanitary Staff at premises after non-notifiable diseases, chiefly Cancer, and the sum of £37 is. od. was received for such disinfection. 409 rooms were disinfected with sulphur in consequence of their verminous condition and 27 lots of verminous bedding disinfected, compared with 618 rooms and 75 lots of bedding in 1913. I have frequently visited the Disinfecting Station during the year, and am able to report that the work has been carried out by the staff to my entire satisfaction, Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 193 The approximate cost of working and maintaining the Disinfecting Station during the past year, including the cost of disinfectants used in fumigating and cleansing rooms, was as follows :— £ s. d. Wages 871 2 10 Fuel 5 8 8 Horse Hire 80 19 0 Stores, Tools, and other materials 60 8 7 Repairs to Horse Vans 13 13 0 Disinfectants, etc. 23 9 2 Repairs to Motor Van 0 6 3 Motor Running Expenses 73 17 0 Lighting 1 6 4 Insurance 9 12 9 Water 4 10 3 Payment to Highways Committee for Steam 30 0 0 £1,174 13 10 The number of lots of bedding stoved was 2,268. Cost per lot of bedding 108. 4d. Cleansing of Persons Act. The baths at the Disinfecting Station have been more used this year, chiefly owing to the increase in the number of contacts with cases of infective diseases. The names of 355 children, 55 belonging to Clapham, two to Putney, 28 to Streatham, 86 to Tooting, and 184 to Wandsworth, stated to be in a verminous condition, were forwarded to me by the Medical Officer, Education Department, London County Council, and the homes were visited by the Inspectors. In the majority of cases only the heads of the children were verminous, but in a few cases the body and clothing were also verminous, 194 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. These children were cleansed by the officials of the London County Council at the Cleansing Station under the supervision of that Authority. 32 adults had baths, 28 were contacts with cases of infective diseases, and four were nurses who had been in attendance in cases of Puerperal Fever. inspection of Urinals in connection with Licensed Premises. The number of urinals inspected was 124, 29 in Clapham, 20 in Putney, 25 in Streatham,10 in Tooting, and 40 in Wandsworth. 514 inspections were made during the year and 25 notices, chiefly for cleansing, were served and complied with. In the Borough there are at present 14 public sanitary conveniences, while there are in addition 21 urinals only belonging to the Council. 190 inspections of the sanitary conveniences for females were made by the female Sanitary Inspectors. The provision of free conveniences for the use of females has been much appreciated, but these entail a greater amount of supervision on the part of the staff employed. 170 inspections have been made during the year by the Inspectors of other sanitary conveniences, chiefly in the elementary schools in the Borough. Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 195 Inspection of Premises where Food is prepared for Sale or Sold. During the year 200 inspections have been made of fried fish shops, 450 of butchers' shops, 577 of greengrocers' shops, and 338 of fishmongers' shops, a total of 1,565. 249 of these inspections were in Clapham, 353 in Putney, 342 in Streatham, 135 in Tooting, and 486 in Wandsworth. Police Court Proceedings. The list which follows shows particulars of Police Court proceedings under the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, during the year. The total amount of fines inflicted was £32 13s. 0d., and the costs £2 12s. od., compared with £15 15s. od. and £3 18s. 6d. in 1913. The majority of the cases were with respect to nuisances or contraventions of By-laws, while one was for exposing unsound food for sale, one for the removal of offensive matter during prohibited hours, and one for selling ice cream from a barrow on which the vendor's name and address was not inscribed. At the close of 1913 there were 381 milkshops on the register, 48 have been added in 1914 and 32 removed, leaving 397 on the Register at the end of 1914. During the year 783 inspections were made of these premises and 22 notices, chiefly for cleansing, were served. Cookson, C. H., 266, Earlsfield Road. (16 cows.) Turner, G. S., Headworth Road. (14 cows.) The total number on the Register at the close of 1914 was 11 and 45 inspections were made. I am able to report that all the above were kept in a satisfactory condition during the year, and it was not necessary to serve any notices. Slaughter-houses. There were 14 Slaughter-houses and one Knacker's Yard on the Register in 1913, one in Clapham was removed, leaving 13 on the Register. The slaughter-house licensed by the London County Council for slaughtering horses for human food was frequently inspected, and during the year 268 horses have been slaughtered on the premises, and all were exported, compared with 281 in 1913. During the year 316 inspections were made of these, but it was only necessary to serve five notices for cleansing. The usual cleansing was carried out by the occupiers at the proper times. Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 201 During the year the Inspectors inspected the carcases of 341 cattle, 2,425 sheep, 237 pigs, and 12 calves in slaughter-houses and butchers' shops, and reported that, with the exception of one pair of lungs, these were all sound when exposed for sale. Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 203 Ice Cream Premises. At the end of 1913 there were 346 of these on the Register. During 1914, 15 were added and 15 removed, leaving a total of 346 on the Register, 531 inspections were made of these premises during the year and 43 notices were served, all of which were for cleansing. Proceedings were instituted against one ice cream vendor for not having his name and address on the barrow. A fine of 3s. with 2s. costs was inflicted. Houses let in Lodgings. At the end of 1913 there were 292 houses let in lodgings on the Register. None were added during 1914, and none removed, making a total of 292 on the Register at the end of 1914. 1,045 inspections of these were made during the year, and 492 notices were served, 17 for overcrowding and 475 for other conditions, chiefly cleansing. On the whole the By-laws have been satisfactorily complied with, although in some instances the cleansing was not carried out at the specified time. Offensive Trade Refuse. I have again to report that the arrangements which have been made by the Council with a contractor for the removal of this refuse have during the year, worked quite satisfactorily, and no complaints have been received. In a certain number of cases this refuse is removed privately, and this has also been carried out in a satisfactory manner. 204 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Unsound Food. 21½ cwt. turnip tops, 234 lbs. tomatoes, 37 lbs. broad beans, 17 boxes pears, three bags walnuts, 23 lbs. skate, one box cods roes, one box flat fish, 10 boxes kippers, one box hake, four boxes haddock, one box mixed fish, one trunk whiting, one carcase and 130 lbs. beef, one cwt. sugar, one case eggs and six livers were destroyed at the request of the owners and the usual certificates granted. FACTORIES AND WORKSHOPS. There has been a decrease in the total number of inspections of the above, compared with 1913, but an examination of the Tables will show that a very large amount of work has been carried out by both the male and female inspectors. I have also this year visited a large number of these premises and am able to report that they are all in a very satisfactory condition. With regard to outworkers it has again been found necessary, as a matter of routine, to forward a warning letter to the majority of employers. The Tables which follow are similar to those used in previous Reports, and the whole of the work done by both male and female Inspectors is there shown in a concise form. The total number of workshops on the Register was 1,741, including 116 retail bakehouses, 129 workshop laundries, 273 dressmakers' and milliners' premises, and 1,223 other workshops, but not including 463 factories, 1,218 workplaces, and 351 outworkers' premises. Including all factories, workshops, workplaces, and outworkers' premises, there were on the Register at the end of 1914, 3,774 premises, compared with 3,774 in 1913. 3.629 in 1912, and 3,470 in 1911. Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 205 The total number of notices served was 364, 354 intimation and 10 statutory, compared with 454 in 1913, 402 in 1912, and 462 in 1911. There were no prosecutions under the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, during the year. Under the head of other workshops are included domestic workshops, and under the head of places where food is prepared for sale are included the kitchens of hotels, restaurants, tripe, fried fish and eel shops, and other places where food is prepared for sale. In all 785 inspections were made of 463 factories, and 62 notices 60 intimation and two statutory, were served. The total number of the workshops on the Register was 1,741, 129 of which were workshop laundries, 116 workshop bakehouses, and 1,467 other workshops. In all 2,649 inspections of these were made, compared with 3,185 in 1913, 3,227 in 1912, and 3,059 in 1911, and 141 intimation and five statutory notices were served. The total number of workplaces on the Register was 1,218 and 1,745 inspections were made, while 132 intimation notices were served, but only three statutory notices were necessary. The total number of defects found was 524, including 22 cases in which there was a breach of special sanitary requirements for bakehouses, compared with 539 and 16 in 1913. To abate these nuisances, 343 notices, 333 intimation and 10 statutory were served, all of which, with the exception of nine were complied with at the end of the year. The nine outstanding were complied with in the first month of this year. Excluding outworkers' premises 524 defects were found and 515 remedied, but only 333 intimation notices were served, as one notice frequently called attention to several defects on the same premises, 206 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. A footnote should be added to show that this has been done. † The figures required in columns 2, 3 and 4 are the total number of the lists received from those employers who comply strictly with the statutory duty of sending two lists each year and of the entries of names of outworkers in those lists. The entries in column 2 must necessarily be even numbers, as there will be two lists for each employer—in some previous returns odd numbers have been inserted. The figures in columns 3 and 4 will usually be (approximately) double of the number of individual outworkers whose names are given, since in the February and August lists of the same employer the same outworker's name will often be repeated. 210 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. In all, 116 lists were received twice in the year, containing the names and addresses of 60 contractors and 349 workmen and seven lists once in the year, containing the names and addresses of three contractors and 62 workmen. There has been a slight increase in the number of outworkers employed by employers in the Borough during the year. The total number of addresses received from other Councils was 507, compared with 521 in 1913, 511 in 1912, and 408 in 1911, and 290 addresses were forwarded to other Councils, compared with 276 in 1913, 285 in 1912, and 251 in 1911. The number of addresses received has decreased by 14 and the number sent has increased by 14. The following are the districts to which lists of outworkers were forwarded, and also the number of outworkers Stepney 56, Battersea 54, Lambeth 46, Croydon 21, City 17, Hammersmith eight, Camberwell six, Southwark five, Winchester and Chelsea four each, Southwark and Kensington three each, Holborn, Worthing, Wimbledon, Hanwell, Eastleigh, East Ham, Willesden, Rochford, Southgate, East Ashford, Shoreditch, Lewisham, Finsbury, Deptford, Stratford, Bermondsey and Bethnal Green two each, West Ham, Walthamstow, Barnes, Stoke Newington, Hampstead, St. Pancras and Bexley one each. 39 names and addresses were forwarded to this Borough in error, and are not included in the above Table. The number of notices sent to employers during the year was 61, compared with 76 in 1913, and these had a most satisfactory result. At the end of 1913 there were 361 outworkers' premises on the Register, 123 were added and 133 removed during the year, leaving 351 on the Reigster at the end of 1914. 541 inspections were made of these premises during the year, and 21 notices, all for cleansing, were served and complied with, 211 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. During the year 15 cases of infective diseases, nine of Scarlet Fever, five of Diphtheria, and one of Erysipelas, were notified as having occurred in the homes of outworkers, compared with 20 in 1913, 16 in 1912, and 15 in 1911. In none of these cases was it necessary to make any order under Section 110 of the Factory and Workshop Act. TABLE CX. 4.—REGISTERED WORKSHOPS. The next Table shows in detail the work of the Inspectors in factories and workshops where males are chiefly employed. The Table shows the work done in each sub-district and is grouped under five divisions: (1) factories, (2) workshops, (3) domestic workshops, (4) workplaces, and (5) outworkers' premises. The total number of inspections was 3,031, compared with 3,510 in 1913, 4,147 in 1912, and 3,020 in 1911, and of re-inspections 745, compared with 732 in 1913, 656, and 1,141, a total of 3,776 compared with 4,242 in the previous year. 1,040 of the inspections and 174 of the re-inspections were in Clapham, 408 and 75 in Putney, 630 and 197 in Streatham, 157 and 51 in Tooting, and 796 and 248 in Wandsworth. No workshops where males were employed were notified to H.M. Inspector, but 26 were reported to this Council by H.M. Inspector, all with the exception of five of these having been previously entered on the Register. In all the workshops under the supervision of the male Inspectors no case of overcrowding was discovered. In 75 of these factories, workshops and workplaces the sanitary conveniences were found defective, in four they were insufficient, and in three they were unsuitable or not separate for the sexes. In 140 the workrooms were in a dirty condition, in four they were insufficiently ventilated, and in 217 other nuisances were found. For these 307 intimation and 10 statutory notices were served, and with the exception of nine intimation notices, were complied with. These notices were complied with in the early part of the year. 213 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. TABLE CXII. Clapham. Putney. Streatham. Tooting. Wandsworth. Total. The total number of premises inspected was 1,829 (441 Clapham, 284 in Putney, 396 in Streatham, 170 in Tooting, and 538 in Wandsworth). 216 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 210 inspections were made of factories, 801 of workshops, 57 of domestic workshops, 392 of workplaces, and 369 of outworkers' premises,' while 247 premises were visited for inquiry and no workroom found. There were only four cases of overcrowding discovered, compared with two in 1913, one in 1912, and three in 1911, and these were at once abated, and 25 were found to be in a dirty condition, compared with 29 in 1913, 37 in 1912, and 17 in 1911. All the factories and workshops inspected during the year had separate water closets for the sexes, but in four factories and five workshops the water closets were defective. Other nuisances were discovered in one workshop, one domestic workshop, 11 workplaces, and eight outworkers' premises, and these were all abated. Table CXV. shows the number of factories, workshops, domestic workshops, and workplaces on the Register at the close of 1913, the number removed from, the number added during 1914, and the number on the Register at the end of 1914. The number of workrooms in workshops is also shown. The factories and workshops are divided into dressmakers' and milliners' premises, laundries, and miscellaneous premises ; and the workplaces are divided into laundries and miscellaneous premises. Of the 106 factories where women are employed, 77 are laun dries and 29 other factories, while of the total workshops, viz.:—495 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 219 273 are dressmakers and milliners, 129 laundries and 93 other workshops, a decrease of 26 dressmakers' and milliners' premises and 16 laundries, compared with 1913, while the number of other workshops is 14 more than in the previous year. The total number of domestic workshops on the Register was 69 (seven in Clapham, eight in Putney, 20 in Streatham, eight in Tooting and 26 in Wandsworth), compared with 63 in 1913. The total number of workplaces on the Register is 357, a decrease of nine compared with 1913, of which 110 are laundries, and 247 miscellaneous premises, chiefly dressmakers and milliners. 220 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Military Billets During the year several premises were taken for the billeting of soldiers, and pickets were stationed at certain places in the Borough. At the request of the Military Authorities, these premises were all inspected weekly and a report on the conditions found sent to the War Department after each inspection. In all 212 inspections were made by the Sanitary Inspectors, (25 in Clapham, 29 in Putney, and 158 in Wandsworth). Refugees' Homes. Several premises were taken by various organisations for the housing of French and Belgian war refugees, and during the year 153 inspections were made of these premises. Six of the inspections were in Clapham, 41 in Streatham, and 106 in Wandsworth. In all these cases the arrangement made for the housing of the refugees were quite satisfactory. Canal Boats Act. During the year 35 inspections of Canal Boats were made, but it was not necessary to serve any notices, as on inspection the conditions of all the boats was found to be satisfactory. Statement of Work done under the Rag Flock Act, 1911. 40 workshops were visited by the Inspector and the materials used for bedding and upholstery were examined. 33 examples were procured and submitted for analysis, 26 of these were reported as complying with the standard of cleanliness required, whilst seven or 27 per cent. were reported against as containing chlorine in excess of the amount permitted, compare with 2,0 per cent. in 1913. and 50 per cent. in 1912. 223 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. In seven cases proceedings were instituted against the person in whose possession the flock was found, with the result that in four cases a small fine was inflicted, in two cases costs were imposed and one case was dismissed with a warning. The total fines and costs amounted to £3. Statement of Work done under the Sale of Pood and Drugs Acts. During the year 1,789 samples of foods and drugs were submitted to the Public Analyst for analysis, compared with 1,849 in 1913, 1,500 in 1912, and 927 in 1911. Of the 1,789 samples analysed 826 were purchased as test or informal samples, while 963 were purchased officially. Of the 963 official samples submitted for analysis 106 or 11 per cent. were reported to be adulterated or not up to standard, and of these samples which were purchased informally or as tests samples 76, or 9.2 per cent. were found adulterated or not up to standard. The total adulterations reported were 182, or 10.2 per cent. of the samples submitted, compared with 11 per cent, in 1913, 18.0 per cent. in 1912, 13.2 per cent. in 1911, and 9.05 per cent. in 1910. The percentage of milk samples found to be adulterated was 7.8, compared with 9.5 in 1913, 10.39 in 1912, and 9.3 in 1911. In 67 out of the 106 cases in which adulterations were detected in the official samples proceedings were instituted against the vendor, compared with 84 in 1913, 86 in 1912, and 77 in 1911. The total amount received in penalties under the above Acts during the year amounted to £'91 4s. od., and the costs to £'38 17s. od., making a total of £130 is. od., compared with £143 7s. 6d. in 1913, £244 14s. in 1912, and £299 19s. 9d. in 1911. 224 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Milk and Cream. MILK. 895 samples of milk were produced for analysis during the year. 67 or 7.48 per cent. were reported against as being adulterated or not up to legal standard. 875 samples were purchased officially, of which 67 or 7.6 per cent. were adulterated, and 20 samples purchased informally, of which four were reported against. 39 samples were found to contain added water, 26 were deficient in milk fat, and two were deficient in milk fat and contained added water. Proceedings were taken in 34 cases, and in 33 cases the Public Health Committee, after considering the amount of adulteration and the circumstances of sale, decided not to prosecute the vendors, but to take further samples. 17 samples of milk were taken on delivery at various Public Institutions situated within the Borough. All these samples were reported to be genuine. 91 samples of milk were procured whilst in transit from the farmer to the retailer, the samples being taken as the milk arrived at various railway stations within the Borough, both at mid-night and mid-day deliveries. Six samples were reported against as containing extraneous water, viz.:—2 per cent., 3 per cent., 4 per cent., 4.5 per cent., 6 per cent. and 6 per cent. respectively. Proceedings were instituted against the farmer of the two last mentioned samples. The summonses were dismissed, the farmer having satisfied the Magistrate that the milk was sold and delivered in the same condition as it came from the cow. Report of the Medical Officer of Health. 231 14 samples of milk were procured during the early morning (from 3 to 4 a.m.), from wholesale dealers whilst delivering milk to the retailer. All these samples were reported to be genuine. Six samples of milk were procured on delivery at private houses, two were reported as being adulterated. The adulteration being small, no proceedings were taken, but the vendor was warned. TABLE CXXIII. Premises. No. of Samples taken. No. Adulterated. Percentage Adulterated. Private Houses 6 2 3.3 162 samples of milk have been taken on Sundays, either in the early morning or at mid-day. 12 or 7.4 per cent. were reported against as being adulterated, compared with 10.6 in 1913, 10 per cent. in 1912, and 10 per cent. in 1911. 351 samples of milk were taken from milk vendors in the street during the early morning (i.e., 5 to 7 a.m.), on week days, and of these 36 or 10.2 per cent. were reported against. 10 samples of milk were taken from automatic milk supply machines and all were reported to be genuine. In two cases proceedings were taken against milk vendors for selling milk from receptacles upon which their name and address were not conspicuously inscribed. (See other offences, Table CXIX.) In 12 cases the defendants relied on a warranty, and in each case the Magistrate was satisfied that the milk sold was in the same condition as received. 232 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Proceedings were taken against a milk carrier for refusing milk for analysis and a penalty of 40s. and costs or one month was imposed. Proceedings were also taken against a milk vendor for wilful obstruction, but as the vendor absconded before the summons was served the case was not dealt with. It is satisfactory to report that not a single sample of milk out of the 875 samples submitted was found to contain a preservative. BUTTER. 478 samples of butter were submitted for analysis during the year, of which 77 or 16.1 per cent. were reported against, compared with 12.67 in 1913, 25.4 per cent. in 1912, 16.4 per cent. in 1911. Of the 478 samples of butter analysed 35 samples were taken officially, 20 or 57 per cent. were reported against, whereas of those samples taken informally 57 or 12.8 per cent. were found to be adulterated. In 19 cases proceedings were instituted against the vendors of the adulterated samples. The penalties and costs amounted to £57 14s. 6d., compared with £50 8s. 0d. in 1913 and £150 6s. 6d. in 1912. Four samples of margarine were submitted for analysis and all returned as genuine. There were four convictions under the Margarine Act, these being in connection with the Sale of Margarine as butter, see Table CXVIII. CHEESE. Six samples of cheese were analysed and all reported to be genuine, 237 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. LARD. 53 samples ol lard were analysed and all reported to be genuine. FLOUR. Three samples of flour were analysed and found to be genuine. COFFEE. 32 samples of coffee were examined, four of which were reported against as containing chicory. In these cases a declaration was made by attaching a label to the tin and no proceedings were taken. COCOA. 21 samples of cocoa were analysed and all reported to be genuine. SUGAR. 28 samples of sugar were analysed, and all reported to be genuine. MUSTARD. 14 samples of mustard were analysed, and all reported to be genuine. PEPPER. 36 samples of Pepper were examined and found genuine. CONFECTIONERY. 13 samples of raspberry jam were analysed, two of which were reported against, one being procured informally and one officially, each sample contained about 5 per cent. apple pulp. 238 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. Proceedings were taken against the vendors who successfully pleaded a warranty given with the jam. Proceedings were then taken against the warrantor who was the manufacturer of the jam for giving a false warranty. At the hearing, the warrantor stated that he was unable to account for the apple pulp found in the jam, and that at the time he gave the warranty, he had every reason to believe that the jam was genuine. The case was dismissed. DRUGS. 83 samples of drugs were analysed, and 11 or 13.2 per cent. were found to be adulterated or not up to the required standard. The samples adulterated were grey powders and prescriptions. Four of the vendors were proceeded against, two for selling a mercury preparation known as grey powder which was deficient in mercury, and two for selling medicine by prescription which had not been properly dispensed as directed by the prescription. The result was that the vendors of the grey powders were ordered to pay costs, and the vendors of Medicine by prescription were convicted and fined 2s. and 18s. costs, and 40s. and 15s. 6d. costs, respectively. OTHER ARTICLES. 106 samples classified under this heading were examined, 17 or 16.0 per cent. being reported against as either adulterated or not up to the required standard. Details of these samples together with the nature of adulteration can be seen on referring to the Report of the Public Analyst annexed. The Inspector who carries out the duties under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts has again performed all these duties in a most thorough and efficient manner, and in addition has satisfactorily carried out all the work in connection with the Rag Flock Act and the Milk and Cream Regulations. 239 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. STAFF. On August 4th, when War was declared, several of the staff of the Public Health Department who were in the Territorial Force were mobilised and since then other members of the staff have joined he forces. The following is a list of those at present serving:— Dr. P. Caldwell Smith, Medical Officer of Health. Dr. F. G. Caley, Tuberculosis Officer. Herbert E. Brown, Sanitary Inspector. Robert Brown, Sanitary Inspector. H. F. P. Holliman, Junior Clerk. E. Hunt, Clerk and Dispenser at Tuberculosis Dispensary. As I was on service near London I was able to keep to some extent in touch with the work. Dr. Oliver Field, who was appointed Deputy Medical Officer of Health, has however, since the middle of August, ably supervised the work of the Department and has been of great service to the other officials in the Department. At the Tuberculosis Dispensary, in the absence of Dr. Caley, Ihe Council appointed Dr. P. Nicol, who has carried out the work at both Dispensaries in a very thorough and satisfactory manner. It was also necessary to obtain the services of a dispenser at Wandsworth as the clerk and dispenser there, who had previously served in the R.A.M.C., rejoined, and has now obtained the rank of Quartermaster in that Corps. To fill the vacancy, Mrs. Nicol was appointed and this arrangement has worked successfully. Another change occurred in the staff of the Department owing to the resignation of the Nurse and the vacancy was filled by the appointment of Miss Moores. Two temporary appointments in the Inspectorial staff were made by the Council and the Inspectors appointed have carried 240 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. out the work of the two Inspectors on military service, while in the clerical staff there was only one vacancy and this has been satisfactorily filled. Up to the end of the year four of the disinfecting staff, (A. Blake, T. Brown, W. H. Brown, and E. Tyler), had been mobilised or joined the forces and some difficulty was experienced in obtaining substitutes, but eventually satisfactory arrangements were made. As far as I am able to judge, and this opinion is corroborated by the Deputy Medical Officer of Health, the work of the Public Health Department of this Borough has not been permitted to fall below the satisfactory standard which has been attained during the time I have had the privilege of being the Medical Officer of Health. With regard to the other members of the staff, I am pleased to report that they have carried out all their duties in a most thorough and conscientious manner, and I cannot but specially mention the Chief Clerk of the Department, Mr. A. E. Cooper, without whose assistance and lengthy experience it would have been more difficult to carry on the general departmental work, and in the preparation of this Report his help has been invaluable. I have the honour to be, Mr. Mayor and Gentlemen, Your obedient Servant, P. CALDWELL SMITH. ANNUAL STATEMENT Of the work done in the Borough of Wandsworth under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts, summarised from the statutory quarterly reports. To the Mayor, Aldermen and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth. Sir and Gentlemen, I have the honour to present the Annual Statement of the work done during the year 1914 under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts. Number of samples submitted. The total number of samples submitted by the Inspector during the year amounted to 1,789. Of these, 963 were taken with the formalities required by the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts, whilst 826 were obtained nformally. The statement following gives the result of analyses of all articles submitted. The nature and extent of the adulteration reported. As regards the milk samples, the greatest adulteration in respect of extraneous water occurred in the case of formal sample No. 90, where it amounted to 18 per cent. The greatest deficiency in milk fat occurred in the case of formal sample No. 38, where it amounted to 97 per cent. Formal samples Nos. 63, 440 and 462 followed closely with a milk fat deficiency of 92, 88, and 73 per cent. respectively. Of the creams purchased as "fresh" 4 samples of the 10 samples submitted were found to contain a boron preservative. The amounts present, expressed in terms of crystallised boric acid, ranged from 0.26 per cent., in the case of both formal samples Nos. 168 and 174, to 0.20 per cent. in the case of formal sample No. 155. Of the cream purchased as "preserved" all 4 samples were found to contain a boron preservative ranging from 0.25 per cent. in the case of formal sample No. 156 to 0.12 per cent. in the case of formal tample No. 158. The fat content of all creams examined ranged from 33.4 per cent. to 62 per cent. The details of all adulterated samples grouped under this heading are given in Table C. The presence of preservatives. All milks were systematically examined for the presence of preservatives, but in no instance was a positive result obtained. The following Table illustrates the number of cases in which preservatives were found in the milk supply of the Borough in this and the three preceding years. Year. Total No. of samples examined. Solids-not-fat 8.82 per cent. Butter. Extent of the adulteration reported. 478 samples of butter were submitted during the year, of which 35 samples were taken with the necessary formalities, whilst 443 were submitted informally, ine total number reported as adulterated, or not up to standard, amounted to 77, or 16.1 per cent. The greatest percentage adulteration occurred in the case of the formal samples, where it amounted to 57.1 per cent., as against 12.8 per cent. for the informal samples. The high percentage in the case of the formal samples, as explained last year, is again due to the fact that formal samples were taken in most instances only when informal sampling showed that systematic adulteration was being practised. In the case of the informal samples the percentage adulteration (12.8) has fallen very considerably from that of the previous year (23.7 per cent.), a result which appears to show that the systematic work carried out in regard to this important article of diet has had a salutary effect in checking adulteration. Nature of the adulteration reported. The nature of the adulteration reported showed that in 38 instances margarine was wholly substituted for butter; in 14 instances mixtures of butter and margarine in varying amounts were sold; and in 25 instances the butter sold contained an excess of boron preservative. Full details of these cases are given in Table D. The presence of preservatives. All samples were examined for the presence of preservatives, with the result that a boron preservative was found in 411 (or 85.9 per cent.) of the samples 251 Report of the Medical Officer of Health. submitted. With the exception of the 25 cases mentioned above, this was present in quantities not exceeding 0.5 per cent.
